13.5016 3.97691 13.4498 3.73411 13.3491C3.49132 13.2485 3.27074 13.1009 3.085 12.915Z"></path></svg></a>What it Does</h2>
<p>The people counter application will demonstrate how to create a smart video IoT solution using Intel® hardware and software tools. The app will detect people in a designated area, providing the number of people in the frame, average duration of people in frame, and total count.</p>

5.49974 6.08518 5.59029 5.66052 5.7662C5.23586 5.94211 4.85001 6.19995 4.525 6.525L2.025 9.02499C1.36858 9.68141 0.999817 10.5717 0.999817 11.5C0.999817 12.4283 1.36858 13.3186 2.025 13.975C2.68141 14.6314 3.57169 15.0002 4.5 15.0002C5.4283 15.0002 6.31858 14.6314 6.975 13.975L8.225 12.725C8.35748 12.5828 8.4296 12.3948 8.42617 12.2005C8.42274 12.0062 8.34403 11.8208 8.20662 11.6834C8.0692 11.546 7.88382 11.4672 7.68952 11.4638C7.49522 11.4604 7.30717 11.5325 7.165 11.665L5.915 12.915C5.72925 13.1009 5.50867 13.2485 5.26588 13.3491C5.02308 13.4498 4.76283 13.5016 4.5 13.5016C4.23716 13.5016 3.97691 13.4498 3.73411 13.3491C3.49132 13.2485 3.27074 13.1009 3.085 12.915Z"></path></svg></a>How it Works</h2>
<p>The counter will use the Inference Engine included in the Intel® Distribution of OpenVINO™ Toolkit. The model used should be able to identify people in a video frame. The app should count the number of people in the current frame, the duration that a person is in the frame (time elapsed between entering and exiting a frame) and the total count of people. It then sends the data to a local web server using the Paho MQTT Python package.</p>
<p>You will choose a model to use and convert it with the Model Optimizer.</p>
<p><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://github.com/sriharsha0806/nd131-openvino-fundamentals-project-starter/blob/master/images/arch_diagram.png"><img src="./IOT_files/arch_diagram.png" alt="architectural diagram" style="max-width:100%;"></a></p>

14.6314 3.57169 15.0002 4.5 15.0002C5.4283 15.0002 6.31858 14.6314 6.975 13.975L8.225 12.725C8.35748 12.5828 8.4296 12.3948 8.42617 12.2005C8.42274 12.0062 8.34403 11.8208 8.20662 11.6834C8.0692 11.546 7.88382 11.4672 7.68952 11.4638C7.49522 11.4604 7.30717 11.5325 7.165 11.665L5.915 12.915C5.72925 13.1009 5.50867 13.2485 5.26588 13.3491C5.02308 13.4498 4.76283 13.5016 4.5 13.5016C4.23716 13.5016 3.97691 13.4498 3.73411 13.3491C3.49132 13.2485 3.27074 13.1009 3.085 12.915Z"></path></svg></a>Install npm</h3>
<p>There are three components that need to be running in separate terminals for this application to work:</p>
<ul>
<li>MQTT Mosca server</li>
<li>Node.js* Web server</li>
<li>FFmpeg server</li>
</ul>
<p>From the main directory:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>For MQTT/Mosca server:</p>
<pre><code>cd webservice/server
npm install
</code></pre>
</li>
<li>
<p>For Web server:</p>
<pre><code>cd ../ui
npm install
</code></pre>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> If any configuration errors occur in mosca server or Web server while using <strong>npm install</strong>, use the below commands:</p>
<pre><code>sudo npm install npm -g 
rm -rf node_modules
npm cache clean
npm config set registry "http://registry.npmjs.org"
npm install
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>

13.5016 3.97691 13.4498 3.73411 13.3491C3.49132 13.2485 3.27074 13.1009 3.085 12.915Z"></path></svg></a>What model to use</h2>
<p>It is up to you to decide on what model to use for the application. You need to find a model not already converted to Intermediate Representation format (i.e. not one of the Intel® Pre-Trained Models), convert it, and utilize the converted model in your application.</p>
<p>Note that you may need to do additional processing of the output to handle incorrect detections, such as adjusting confidence threshold or accounting for 1-2 frames where the model fails to see a person already counted and would otherwise double count.</p>
<p><strong>If you are otherwise unable to find a suitable model after attempting and successfully converting at least three other models</strong>, you can document in your write-up what the models were, how you converted them, and why they failed, and then utilize any of the Intel® Pre-Trained Models that may perform better.</p>

13.5016 3.97691 13.4498 3.73411 13.3491C3.49132 13.2485 3.27074 13.1009 3.085 12.915Z"></path></svg></a>Setup the environment</h4>
<p>You must configure the environment to use the Intel® Distribution of OpenVINO™ toolkit one time per session by running the following command:</p>
<pre><code>source /opt/intel/openvino/bin/setupvars.sh -pyver 3.5
</code></pre>
<p>You should also be able to run the application with Python 3.6, although newer versions of Python will not work with the app.</p>

13.5016 3.97691 13.4498 3.73411 13.3491C3.49132 13.2485 3.27074 13.1009 3.085 12.915Z"></path></svg></a>Running on the CPU</h4>
<p>When running Intel® Distribution of OpenVINO™ toolkit Python applications on the CPU, the CPU extension library is required. This can be found at:</p>
<pre><code>/opt/intel/openvino/deployment_tools/inference_engine/lib/intel64/
</code></pre>
<p><em>Depending on whether you are using Linux or Mac, the filename will be either <code>libcpu_extension_sse4.so</code> or <code>libcpu_extension.dylib</code>, respectively.</em> (The Linux filename may be different if you are using a AVX architecture)</p>
<p>Though by default application runs on CPU, this can also be explicitly specified by <code>-d CPU</code> command-line argument:</p>
<pre><code>python main.py -i resources/Pedestrian_Detect_2_1_1.mp4 -m your-model.xml -l /opt/intel/openvino/deployment_tools/inference_engine/lib/intel64/libcpu_extension_sse4.so -d CPU -pt 0.6 | ffmpeg -v warning -f rawvideo -pixel_format bgr24 -video_size 768x432 -framerate 24 -i - http://0.0.0.0:3004/fac.ffm
</code></pre>
<p>If you are in the classroom workspace, use the “Open App” button to view the output. If working locally, to see the output on a web based interface, open the link <a href="http://0.0.0.0:3004/" rel="nofollow">http://0.0.0.0:3004</a> in a browser.</p>

13.5016C4.23716 13.5016 3.97691 13.4498 3.73411 13.3491C3.49132 13.2485 3.27074 13.1009 3.085 12.915Z"></path></svg></a>Running on the Intel® Neural Compute Stick</h4>
<p>To run on the Intel® Neural Compute Stick, use the <code>-d MYRIAD</code> command-line argument:</p>
<pre><code>python3.5 main.py -d MYRIAD -i resources/Pedestrian_Detect_2_1_1.mp4 -m your-model.xml -pt 0.6 | ffmpeg -v warning -f rawvideo -pixel_format bgr24 -video_size 768x432 -framerate 24 -i - http://0.0.0.0:3004/fac.ffm
</code></pre>
<p>To see the output on a web based interface, open the link <a href="http://0.0.0.0:3004/" rel="nofollow">http://0.0.0.0:3004</a> in a browser.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The Intel® Neural Compute Stick can only run FP16 models at this time. The model that is passed to the application, through the <code>-m &lt;path_to_model&gt;</code> command-line argument, must be of data type FP16.</p>
<h4><a id="user-content-using-a-camera-stream-instead-of-a-video-file" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" 5.49974C6.54034 5.49974 6.08518 5.59029 5.66052 5.7662C5.23586 5.94211 4.85001 6.19995 4.525 6.525L2.025 9.02499C1.36858 9.68141 0.999817 10.5717 0.999817 11.5C0.999817 12.4283 1.36858 13.3186 2.025 13.975C2.68141 14.6314 3.57169 15.0002 4.5 15.0002C5.4283 15.0002 6.31858 14.6314 6.975 13.975L8.225 12.725C8.35748 12.5828 8.4296 12.3948 8.42617 12.2005C8.42274 12.0062 8.34403 11.8208 8.20662 11.6834C8.0692 11.546 7.88382 11.4672 7.68952 11.4638C7.49522 11.4604 7.30717 11.5325 7.165 11.665L5.915 12.915C5.72925 13.1009 5.50867 13.2485 5.26588 13.3491C5.02308 13.4498 4.76283 13.5016 4.5 13.5016C4.23716 13.5016 3.97691 13.4498 3.73411 13.3491C3.49132 13.2485 3.27074 13.1009 3.085 12.915Z"></path></svg></a>Using a camera stream instead of a video file</h4>
<p>To get the input video from the camera, use the <code>-i CAM</code> command-line argument. Specify the resolution of the camera using the <code>-video_size</code> command line argument.</p>
<p>For example:</p>
<pre><code>python main.py -i CAM -m your-model.xml -l /opt/intel/openvino/deployment_tools/inference_engine/lib/intel64/libcpu_extension_sse4.so -d CPU -pt 0.6 | ffmpeg -v warning -f rawvideo -pixel_format bgr24 -video_size 768x432 -framerate 24 -i - http://0.0.0.0:3004/fac.ffm
</code></pre>
<p>To see the output on a web based interface, open the link <a href="http://0.0.0.0:3004/" rel="nofollow">http://0.0.0.0:3004</a> in a browser.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong>
User has to give <code>-video_size</code> command line argument according to the input as it is used to specify the resolution of the video or image file.</p>

13.5016 3.97691 13.4498 3.73411 13.3491C3.49132 13.2485 3.27074 13.1009 3.085 12.915Z"></path></svg></a>A Note on Running Locally</h2>
<p>The servers herein are configured to utilize the Udacity classroom workspace. As such,
to run on your local machine, you will need to change the below file:</p>
<pre><code>webservice/ui/src/constants/constants.js
</code></pre>
<p>The <code>CAMERA_FEED_SERVER</code> and <code>MQTT_SERVER</code> both use the workspace configuration.
You can change each of these as follows:</p>
<pre><code>CAMERA_FEED_SERVER: "http://localhost:3004"
...
MQTT_SERVER: "ws://localhost:3002"
</code></pre>
